## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: The task involves the rate of change of concentration (dA_dt) as a function of time (t) and concentration (A), which is the core of reaction rate laws in chemical kinetics. The physical relationships typically reflect how the reaction rate depends on reactant concentration (order of reaction) or time-dependent rate coefficients.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration, e.g., surface catalysis under saturation)
- First-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A (exponential decay of reactant)
- Second-order reaction (dimerization): dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular rate law)
- nth-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (power-law, fractal kinetics or complex order)
- Half-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * sqrt(A) (chain reaction with termination)
- Autocatalytic rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic growth in autocatalysis)
- Parallel first- and second-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (parallel reactions of different molecularities)
- Reversible first-order (fixed total): dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A (linear offset from reverse reaction)
- Time-dependent rate coefficient (exponential): dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (catalyst deactivation or activation)
- Time-dependent rate coefficient (power-law): dA_dt = c0 * t**c1 * A (gradual deactivation)
- Substrate inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2) (excess substrate inhibition)
- Linear combination with time: dA_dt = c0 * t + c1 * A (mixed time and concentration dependence)
- Exponential concentration dependence: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * A) (highly nonlinear, nucleation-like)
- Self-catalyzed with inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) / (1 + c2 * A) (autocatalysis with saturation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Constant rate irrespective of A implies zero-order kinetics, typically from surface saturation or constant light flux in photochemistry.
- Rate linearly proportional to A indicates a unimolecular or pseudo-first-order elementary step.
- Rate proportional to A² suggests a bimolecular collision mechanism (dimerization).
- Rate proportional to A*(c - A) is the signature of an autocatalytic process where product drives further reaction (logistic behavior).
- Denominator containing 1 + c₁A + c₂A² points to substrate inhibition, where excess substrate reduces rate.
- Time multiplied by A (e.g., dA/dt ∝ t^p A) implies a time-varying rate constant, modeling catalyst aging or external condition drift.
- Fractional powers of A (e.g., sqrt(A)) indicate non-elementary kinetics, such as chain reactions with termination steps or fractal diffusion.
- Sum of two terms (e.g., c₀A + c₁A²) signals parallel reaction pathways with different molecularities.
- An additive constant in dA/dt (c₀ + c₁A) suggests a background process or reversible reaction with a constant product pool.
- Exponential dependence on A (exp(cA)) hints at extreme sensitivity, as in autocatalytic explosion or nucleation events.
